Chinese Ratepayers Association Elected Officers Yesterday 78

▲ Wang Xiaolai and Xu Jiqing as Chairman and Vice Chairman

▲ Hu Mengjia, Lu Feibo Hong, etc. as Standing Committee Members

The Shanghai Ratepayers Association held its first meeting of the ninth executive committee at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee meeting hall at 3:00 PM yesterday. Executive committee members Li Bohan, Hu Fengxiang, Ye Fuxiao (representing Hu Fengxiang), Hu Mengjia, Lu Fengzhu, Xu Jiqing, Cheng Xiechun, Fang Jiaobo, Chu Huiseng, Wang Xiaolai, Jiang Yiping, Yu Xiji, Zhang Yichen, Xie Zhongfu, Tu Kaizheng, Hu Xisheng, Zhu Yinjiang, Yuan Jinchu, Sun Jingxi, Shen Tianxin, and Wu Yaqin attended. Directors Liu Hongsheng and alternate executive committee member Sun Qiuping attended as observers. Wang Xiaolai was elected as the temporary chairman. After the meeting began, the case of Yan Ersheng resigning as an executive committee member was discussed. It was resolved that the executive committee members are elected by the delegates' assembly, and the executive committee has no right to accept the resignation. Then, one chairman and one vice chairman, and three standing committee members were elected. Yuan Jinchu and Zhang Yichen were designated by the temporary chairman to count and announce the votes. As a result of the vote count, Wang Xiaolai received fifteen votes and was elected as the chairman. Xu Jiqing received thirteen votes and was elected as the vice chairman. Hu Mengjia and Lu Feibo Hong each received fourteen votes, and Yuan Jinchu received eleven votes, and they were elected as standing committee members. After the election was completed, the proposal to revise the association's rules and review methods was discussed. It was resolved that Jiang Yiping, Sun Jingxi, Shen Tianxin, Cheng Xiechun, and Yuan Jinchu be appointed as members to form a review committee, and Yuan Jinchu was appointed as the convener. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Westerners' Special Meeting 79

▲ Scheduled to be held on May 2nd

▲ Petition will be sent out on Tuesday

Most foreigners in this city consider the Western taxpayers' annual meeting held on Wednesday to have made a serious mistake by rashly rejecting the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors in the Public Concession. Moreover, they believe that the number of people present at the meeting, only over two hundred, is not enough to be a true representative assembly. Now, in order to remedy the spirit of Sino-foreign cooperation, they have decided to convene a special meeting to resubmit the proposal for voting. According to reliable sources from the Western community, the special meeting is currently scheduled to be held on May 2nd at the City Hall. Although the date of the meeting is not yet formally decided, the majority of those involved believe that that day is the most suitable. Because that day is Friday, after that it will be Saturday and Sunday, and later, the three days from May 5th to 7th will be the Spring Racing season. There is even less certainty of obtaining the quorum for the meeting. Therefore, if the special meeting cannot be held on May 2nd, it will inevitably be postponed for a week until May 9th before it can be convened. This will inevitably lead to complications and make the deadlock that has already been formed even more difficult to resolve. Due to the rule that a meeting cannot be held until ten days after the notice, it is also impossible to hold it earlier. Due to various reasons, the meeting date of May 2nd is generally expected to become a reality. As for the petition to convene the special meeting, the joint signatures of twenty-five taxpayers are still being negotiated. It is expected that there will be ten to fifteen British, five Americans, five Japanese, and five Europeans to support it. Recently, due to the Easter holiday, many Westerners are on vacation. Although many have already verbally agreed, it will take at least until Monday tomorrow to complete the formalities for obtaining twenty-five signatures on the petition. At that time, the petition will be led by the President of the British Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Marshall, and will be directly submitted to the Consular Body on Tuesday. On the same day, the Consular Body will convene a meeting of the Consular Body and formally announce the convening of the special meeting in the name of all the consuls of various countries in this city. Important figures from the foreign community now only hope that the Chinese community will understand and avoid causing unexpected disturbances so that the special meeting will not be adjourned due to a lack of quorum.

The Great American Evening News stated that the weakness of a representative government is that it cannot represent the views of the entire body. No matter how carefully a legislative body deliberates, it may sometimes be manipulated by a minority. This kind of bad phenomenon occurs from time to time in legislative bodies around the world. Unfortunately, the Western taxpayers' meeting also turned into the same unfortunate event by rejecting the Chinese directors' case. Since the rejection problem occurred, this newspaper believes that this move was unexpected and very surprising, so it tried its best to solicit the opinions of people from all countries in Shanghai. As a result, it was found that the public did not agree with the rejection. On the day of the meeting, very few people attended. Those who were absent did not pay attention to the proposal. Most thought that everyone knew the benefits of the problem, so it would be easy to pass, so there was no need to personally attend the meeting and vote in favor. However, this idea was not perfect. As a taxpayer, one should respect legislative rights, attend meetings, and exercise their rights in order to avoid being manipulated. Now, because of the absence of these people, the Chinese directors' case was rejected, then those who were absent must bear some responsibility. As for those who attended, some originally intended to support the Works Bureau's proposal, but after hearing McDonald's sophistry, they did not know how to refute it, thinking that the full reasons for the proposal would not be subdued by McDonald's remarks, so they did not bother to argue with him. The most surprising thing is that some taxpayers who attended the meeting did vote against it at the time, but later realized their mistake and regretted it. According to what this newspaper knows, the error of the rejection is now being corrected, but the procedures are not easy. A special meeting cannot be convened unless two-thirds of the number attend. Although it concerns the interests of the entire city of Shanghai, the leaders of the foreign community in Shanghai will definitely come forward to plan and ensure that the special meeting is established to make up for past mistakes. In short, people from all countries in Shanghai recognize this rejection as a major unfortunate event. It is hoped that the Chinese community will recognize the truth and not allow a small number of foreigners' blind actions to cause unexpected damage to the good friendship between China and foreign countries.

Chinese and Japanese Silk and Other Goods Should Be Mutually Beneficial 82

▲ National Goods Maintenance Association Cables the Foreign Ministry

The China National Goods Maintenance Association yesterday cabled the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating: Wang Junjian, Minister of Foreign Affairs, Executive Yuan, National Government of the Capital, on the twelfth of this month, a telegram was sent, requesting your wise consideration. For many days, no instructions have been received, causing deep anxiety. It is believed that at the time of the revision and signing of the Sino-Japanese Commercial Treaty, if Chinese goods that are sold well in Japan and South Korea, such as silk satin, gauze, summer cloth, porcelain, sundries, and medicinal materials, can be included in the mutual benefit, and the tax rates are the same as those for Japanese goods entering China, then although our country's industry and commerce have previously lost the East, we can still recover the mulberry elm in the West. And the foreign trade, which has been rejected by Japan's harsh taxes, can also be slightly saved. Otherwise, Japanese goods are transported to China, and we give them favorable light taxes, while Chinese silk, etc., are transported to Japan and South Korea, and still heavily taxed, and there is no change. For seven or eight years, we have been running around and appealing, with a glimmer of hope in this revision of the commercial treaty, and we are afraid that we will still be disappointed as before. The issue of revising the commercial treaty, which is closely related to the strength and decline of society and the country, has not given the industrial and commercial circles the opportunity to participate in the discussion. After the other party brazenly announced it, our foreign affairs authorities remained silent and kept it secret. What is the meaning of this kind of revolutionary diplomacy and the people's livelihood doctrine? Our association has repeatedly received letters and telegrams from various groups such as silk, summer cloth, and porcelain from various places, inquiring about what goods are included in the mutual benefit agreement in the new Sino-Japanese Commercial Treaty. If our Chinese goods can be included in the mutual benefit when transported to Japan and South Korea, and can be the same as the tax rules for Japanese goods entering China, then we should quickly prepare and refine the products in order to restore the sales in Japan and South Korea and continue business. If we miss the opportunity to revise the treaty this time and repeat the mistakes, benefiting them but not benefiting us, then not only will there be no hope of recovery for Chinese silk, etc., and the country will be in danger of perishing, but also a bad precedent will be set, and various countries will follow suit, and the international status will be permanently lost to the bottom of the sea, harming the party and the country without end. Our association is anxious like fire, not considering the trouble, and forced to telegraph again to appeal, hoping that the lords will approve the acceptance and must achieve equal tax rules for both Chinese and Japanese silk and various goods. Otherwise, do not sign, and ask for immediate implementation and prompt instructions, which will be a great convenience for the people of the country. Wang Jiean, Wang Xingyi, and Wang Hanqiang, Standing Committee Members of the China National Goods Maintenance Association, respectfully request.

Record of the Shanghai Municipal Executive Committee's Regular Meeting 84

▲ The Seventh Meeting

The Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee held its seventh regular meeting yesterday, chaired by Fan Zhengbo. The summary of the motions is recorded below:

▲ Matters for Discussion: (1) The Second District Party Headquarters submitted a request on behalf of the Fourth Branch to require political guarantors for students in secondary schools and above, to investigate the case of Huang Zeshang’s injury. It was resolved to submit it to the Central Committee. (2) The Fourth District Party Headquarters submitted a request to forward to the Central Committee a request to the Judicial Yuan of the National Government to order the Shanghai Special District Local Court to severely punish reactionaries caught in the Shanghai International Settlement. It was resolved to investigate and reply. (3) The Fourth District Party Headquarters submitted a request to forward to the Central Committee a request to the National Government to order all shipyards to equip merchant ships to be able to be converted to warships in the future. It was resolved to forward it to the Central Committee. (4) The Fifth District Party Headquarters submitted a request to forward the matter of the Japanese fleet conducting spring maneuvers in China, infringing upon national rights. It was resolved to forward it to the Central Committee. (5) The Sixth District Party Headquarters submitted a request stating that the Japanese navy's spring maneuvers in Zhoushan infringe upon China's maritime rights, requesting an immediate telegram to the Central Committee for a serious protest and immediate forceful restraint to safeguard national rights. It was resolved to forward it together with the previous case. (6) The Student Union submitted a request to forward to the Central Committee a protest against Japan increasing troops in Manchuria and Mongolia. It was resolved to forward it to the Central Committee. (7) Comrade Bao Rong's review report stated that the organizational regulations of the Training Department of this committee, which were submitted for review, have been reviewed and are deemed appropriate and should be passed. It was requested to be reviewed and discussed, and it was resolved to pass it. (8) The Civil Training Committee proposed to appoint Comrade Zhang Xingfu as an assistant staff member of the General Affairs Section of this committee. It was resolved to pass it. (9) The Training Department proposed to forward a request from the training committee of the Sixth District regarding the incomplete implementation of the regulations on punishing staff for using foreign goods, earnestly requesting their adoption and implementation to uphold Party discipline. It was resolved to hand it over to Comrade Chen Dezheng for review together with other cases.

▲ Temporary Motions: (1) The Executive Committee members of this committee should take an oath of office on a regular basis. (Resolution) It was decided to take the oath of office at 10:00 a.m. on April 28th, together with the Supervisory Committee members. (2) In the Yong'an Textile Factory bribery case, the Local Court has already ruled that Tan Huanxiang and others should not be prosecuted. This committee has already applied to the court for reconsideration. Should we further consult the Central Committee to have guidelines to follow? (Resolution) Consult the Central Committee. (3) The annual meeting of foreign taxpayers in the International Settlement rejected the increase in the number of Chinese directors on the Municipal Council. How should this committee awaken the public to fight together? (Measures) (1) Request the Central Committee to order the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to actively pursue the recovery of the Shanghai International Settlement and issue a declaration to all public organizations to advocate together. (2) Before this case is properly resolved, (A) the Chinese taxpayers' association in the Settlement should elect eleven more directors to the Settlement municipal authorities to form a board of directors to handle Chinese affairs; (B) starting from this month, the taxes paid by the Settlement residents should be decided by the Chinese taxpayers' conference to designate a bank for uniform deposit, and should not be handed over to the Municipal Council again. (3) All properties of Chinese people in the Settlement that are registered under the names of foreign merchants and have obtained deed certificates should be canceled and re-registered with the domestic land administrative agencies to obtain land business licenses. (4) Lawyer Macdonald should apologize to the Chinese directors. (5) Issue a declaration stating that the increase in the number of Chinese directors does not require the approval of the foreign taxpayers' association, so the argument of convening a special meeting of foreign taxpayers to seek remedies should not be accepted. (Resolution) Passed. (4) The Training Department proposed that Comrade Pei Cheng of the Secretariat of this department is currently unable to report to work due to illness, and it is proposed to appoint Comrade Jiang Huaishu as an agent. Please approve the case. (Resolution) Passed.

Investigation of the Case of Selling National Land Yesterday 90

▲ Ma Wenxiang Detained

Xin Shanghai News reported that more than 200 acres of Pudong Gaohang District Pubin Dangtian, which belonged to Shanghai City, were fraudulently sold to a certain foreign firm by Ma Wenxiang in collusion with local people, forging field deeds, and obscuring the facts. Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., the court specially summoned both parties to the Sixth Criminal Court for investigation by Inspector Yang Wenjun. The plaintiffs were Yu Zhenhui and Qu Xing, representatives of the Eleventh District Branch, and the defendant was Ma Wenxiang, and five or six witnesses who were also involved in the sale. Inspector Yang prohibited the public from attending the hearing because the case was under investigation. The investigation resulted in the detention of Ma Wenxiang. In the next few days, he will personally go to the district to verify the facts before making a decision.

Provisional Regulations on Commodity Inspection 92

▲ The Municipal Government Orders the Social Affairs Bureau and the Business and Industry Reorganization Committee to Take Note

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce promulgated the Provisional Regulations on Commodity Export Inspection a year ago. In view of the difficulties in legal application and the lack of thoroughness in practical implementation, the Ministry has revised the aforementioned regulations into the Provisional Regulations on Commodity Inspection after considering past situations. Yesterday, the municipal government approved the Ministry's consultation and forwarding of a copy of the revised regulations, requesting that the relevant departments be notified. The Social Affairs Bureau and the Business and Industry Reorganization Committee of this city have been instructed to take note. The text of the regulations is extracted below: Article 1. All domestic and imported commodities that need to be inspected shall be inspected in accordance with these regulations. Article 2. Commodities with one of the following conditions shall be inspected: (1) those with accumulated malpractices of counterfeiting; (2) those with potential toxicity or danger; (3) those requiring identification of their quality grade. Article 3. The types of commodities to be inspected shall be determined by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Article 4. Commodity inspection shall be conducted at the location of export or import. However, at the request of the merchant or when the Ministry of Industry and Commerce deems it necessary, it may be conducted at the distribution market. Article 5. Commodities that are subject to inspection shall not be exported, imported, or traded without inspection and a certificate. Article 6. Foreign commodities that are subject to inspection and hold a certificate of inspection from the country of origin may be exempted from inspection, but if they are found to be inconsistent with the original certificate, they shall still be inspected. Article 7. The standards for qualification of various commodities shall be separately determined by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Article 8. A fee may be charged for inspecting commodities, and the amount of the fee shall be separately determined by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for each commodity. Article 9. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce shall establish commodity inspection bureaus at the locations of commodity inspection to carry out inspection affairs. The organization of the commodity inspection bureau shall be determined by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Article 10. Commodities that are subject to inspection shall be reported by the merchant to the local commodity inspection bureau for inspection before export, import, or trade. Article 11. When inspecting commodities, samples shall be taken, and the quantity shall be separately determined by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for each commodity. Article 12. Samples shall be taken by the commodity inspection bureau, and merchants shall not designate them. Article 13. For commodities that pass the inspection, the commodity inspection bureau shall issue a certificate; for those that fail, a copy of the inspection report shall be attached to notify the original applicant. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce shall separately determine the validity period of the certificate. Article 14. Commodities that have been inspected may be re-inspected once at the request of the original applicant within the validity period, without additional fees. Article 15. If the certificate is lost, the applicant shall apply for a replacement certificate. If the shipping schedule changes or the packaging changes, the original applicant shall apply for a replacement certificate, but both must be accompanied by accurate reasons and approved by the commodity inspection bureau. Article 16. Merchants who offer bribes when applying for inspection or alter the certificate after inspection shall be punished in accordance with the relevant articles of the Criminal Law. The same shall apply to personnel of the commodity inspection bureau who are guilty of dereliction of duty or accepting bribes. Article 17. Merchants who violate Article 10 of these regulations shall be fined up to 500 yuan and ordered to report for inspection. Article 18. Merchants who privately exchange goods or change the quantity after commodity inspection shall be fined up to 300 yuan. Article 19. If the packaging is changed without the approval of the commodity inspection bureau after the commodity inspection certificate is issued, it must be re-inspected. Article 20. If the personnel performing the inspection deliberately harm the merchants when taking samples, they shall be reported by others and punished by the commodity inspection bureau. Article 21. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce may formulate various separate regulations for the implementation of inspection. Article 22. Commodity inspection bureaus may formulate various detailed rules or measures as needed for the implementation of inspection, but they must be submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval. Article 23. These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation.

Municipal Public Security Bureau Seizes Reactionary Propaganda Agency 93

Director Yuan of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, having repeatedly received secret orders from the Central Committee to investigate and ban reactionary propaganda agencies, specifically ordered the supervisory office to select capable staff to conduct investigations in all directions. They also arrested seven reactionary suspects: Tong Meifa, 52 years old, from Ningbo; Liang Minzhu, 20 years old, from Hangzhou; Qiu Zijun, 18 years old, from Shaoxing; Hu Shichuan, 19 years old, from Anhui; Ni Diqi, 17 years old; Sun Hutang, 18 years old, from Jiaxing; and Zhao Yu, 16 years old, from Yancheng. The Municipal Public Security Bureau specially brought the suspects in for interrogation. Liang Minzhu signed and confirmed that the Revolutionary Daily was indeed printed by Minyou before the 16th. The Municipal Public Security Bureau, together with the French Concession Police, has closed the printing office and is strictly pursuing the main offenders.

Wusong Poor People's Lending Office Established 95

The Wusong District Poor People's Lending Office and Agricultural Lending Office, under the direction of Liu Ziwen, a member of the Wusong Municipal Committee, appointed Gu Xiyuan as the director to start preparations. The organization has been completed and will be officially established today (the 20th). The office is attached to the Municipal Committee Office. It is stipulated that the 5th and 10th of each month are the dates for lending and repaying loans. Each poor person is limited to a loan of five yuan, to be repaid in ten installments, one installment every five days. Farmers are limited to a loan of twelve yuan, with a weekly interest rate of eight li. The Municipal Committee Office is deeply concerned that the poor farmers in the district may not understand the truth, so they posted notices and distributed leaflets everywhere yesterday, and ordered the local headmen to publicize widely, so that those who can borrow loans will be enthusiastic.

Investigation of the Disaster Situation in Various Counties of Shaanxi Province 96

▲ The Disaster Situation is Tragic, Heartbreaking to Hear

▲ It is Resolved that the Distribution of Relief Funds Should be Expedited

News from the Shanghai Office of the Relief Committee: The disaster situation in Shaanxi Province is becoming increasingly severe. The following is a summary of the report from the Shaanxi Disaster Situation News Agency: (1) After the snow melted in Wugong County, human bones were found everywhere. The county relief branch is digging pits to bury them. The number of people who starved to death can be seen from this. The daughter-in-law of the Dai family in Shejiabao, Baiyangzhai, was only twenty years old. Both her parents-in-law starved to death, leaving only her husband and a one-year-old daughter. Unable to make a living and her husband being ill, she sold herself again for six silver dollars. The daughter-in-law breastfed her daughter before leaving, tears streaming down her face, reluctant to leave. Then, she jumped into a well. The well was 25 feet deep. She was pulled out, but not dead. Hundreds of women in the county are being sold out of the province every day. The tragic scene is truly rare. (2) Hua County is a small place with a dense population and little production of beans and wheat. People mostly rely on planting timber and mountain fruits for a living. Last winter, the snow fell two feet, and the sun was not seen for three months. There has never been such severe cold in a hundred years, and all the trees have withered. The county originally had 141,058 people, and 35,832 people have died. Thousands of people are buried in mounds of graves. The surviving victims cannot even get a single meal of bran a day. Since the beginning of spring, the epidemic has been spreading. Victims on the verge of death die even faster if they contract the epidemic. The number of deaths in recent days is truly alarming. (3) The disaster situation in Mei County is extremely tragic. The original population was 90,746, and 69,293 people have died. More than 2,100 households have been wiped out. Many victims are fleeing to Xinghan. Most of the houses have been demolished. More than 200 villages in the county, dozens of villages south of the official road, are uninhabited. The fields are barren, and Artemisia are forming forests. There is land but no one to plant it, and those who have people do not have cattle or seeds. Even if there is ample rain, the fields are still barren. It is feared that even after twenty years, the vitality will be difficult to restore. (4) The National Government has resolved to allocate 300,000 yuan for relief in Shaanxi. It is hoped that the Ministry of Finance will be able to understand the government's intention to save the victims and will be able to find a way to allocate the funds as soon as possible. The Shaanxi Provincial Relief Association's telegram to Yu Youren is recorded below: Mr. Yu, I have received your telegram. Your proposal to allocate funds for relief in Shaanxi has been resolved and handed over to the Ministry of Finance to allocate 300,000 yuan. I am deeply moved by your concern for your hometown and your compassion for the hungry. It is now a time when the old harvest is gone and the new harvest is not yet in. With this relief, the general victims can celebrate their rebirth. Please expedite the distribution to provide emergency relief. Thank you in advance. The Shaanxi Provincial Relief Association bows.

Yu Youren Mourns the Disaster in Shaanxi 97

▲ Marks His Birthday with Mourning

This month, the 18th, was Yu Youren's 53rd birthday. Many of his fellow villagers gathered at his residence in Shanghai, intending to offer him congratulations. Yu believed that the disaster situation in Shaanxi was urgent, people were dying every day, and his heart was troubled by the disaster area, so he refused to allow celebrations and instructed his secretary to issue a notice. All fellow villagers who came were given a black gauze to attach to their sleeves to commemorate the people who died of starvation in the disaster. On this day, although many guests gathered in Yu's residence, the atmosphere was solemn and everyone was sadly thinking of the famine-stricken hometown. The notice from his secretary is recorded below: Today we respectfully wish Mr. Yu Youren a happy birthday. Mr. Yu believes that the disaster situation in Shaanxi is tragic, and more than two million people are starving to death, but no relief has been provided. He is exhausted and feels extremely painful. Fellow villagers have come, but he could not stop them. Mr. Yu feels extremely uneasy and specially requested that black gauze be prepared for fellow villagers to wear to express their sorrow for the people who died of starvation in their hometown. It is also to remind his colleagues to be vigilant about disasters. Mr. Yu and his family will all follow this, and he ordered that this intention be conveyed. I hope that my fellow villagers will understand. On this day, everything Yu discussed was related to disaster relief, and those who heard it were solemn.

The Ministry of Communications Rejects the Postal Workers Union's Salary Increase 102

The Shanghai Postal Workers Union previously stated that the customs employees had increased their salaries and that the treatment was unfair. It requested the General Post Office to forward a request to the Ministry of Communications for an improvement plan and to increase the salary subsidies for compensation. It is now known that the bureau received an order from the Ministry of Communications yesterday rejecting the request. The original order stated: Upon investigation, postal workers have repeatedly requested improvements in their treatment due to unfair treatment. This ministry has adopted a compromise method to revise it separately. Although the salaries of senior personnel have been slightly reduced, the treatment of general staff is indeed better than before. It is certainly not the case that the cost of living is increasing, and the impact is not only on postal personnel. It has not been heard that any agency has requested to revise their salaries as a result. The donations are prepared by the Central Party Department for special funds for party member compensation. All personnel serving the party and the country cannot violate party orders and delay payment. All agencies are now paying uniformly and there is no additional subsidy as a result. The amount to be paid is based on the salary as a ratio, and those with lower salaries are not required to pay, so there is no impact on livelihoods. The post office is a state-run transportation business and is similar in nature to the road and telecommunications administrations. The customs has special circumstances. How can the Postal Workers Union, which once belonged to the customs, use the same origin as an excuse to compare everything? The request to increase the salary rate or subsidy should not be discussed. You should check and inform them accordingly.

The Flourishing Real Estate Business in This Port

▲ Land Prices Rise

The *Da Wan Bao* reports that many important figures in the real estate industry expect that real estate transactions in Shanghai will become increasingly prosperous, and that their value will soon double. For example, a vacant lot on Avenue Joffre that was recently worth 185,000 yuan has now risen to over 200,000 yuan. It is said that since the beginning of January this year, a large number of real estate transactions, both large and small, have been concluded, and their total value has far exceeded that of the same period last year. This is because there is a large amount of silver stored in the Shanghai market, the price of silver is low, and the exchange rate is unfavorable, so people are investing in real estate. In addition, many people from the interior are moving to Shanghai due to local unrest, and the population of this port has greatly increased, so there is more cash and purchasing power, which is said to be one of the reasons for the rapid increase in real estate prices.

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Changes the Pricing Method for Ship License Plates and Lights

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities handles the registration of cargo ships. Originally, each ship had to obtain two license plates, one for the hull and one for the seat, and four inlaid wooden strips, and pay a deposit of four yuan for the license plates. The pricing method for returning or reissuing license plates and lights was also determined according to this amount. Now, the deposit for the license plates has been changed to three yuan, but the previously determined pricing method has not been changed. Therefore, if a shipowner obtains a full set, he only pays three yuan, but if he returns them separately, he can get four yuan, and some unscrupulous people inevitably take advantage of this. The municipal treasury suffers a loss. Therefore, the bureau submitted a request to the central government a few days ago to set a new pricing method, namely, two yuan for the return of two license plates, six jiao for one light, eight fen for one light seat, and three jiao two fen for four inlaid strips, totaling three yuan. However, if they are lost and need to be reissued, the cost is higher due to piecemeal preparation, and to warn people to use them carefully, the price of each item is slightly higher, namely, two yuan eight jiao for two license plates, seven jiao for one light, one jiao for one light seat, and four jiao for four inlaid strips, totaling four yuan. All shipping offices have been ordered to comply.

Automobile Driver's License

▲ Should Be Sent to the Bureau of Public Utilities for Review

Article 8 of the Municipal Regulations for the Management of Automobile Drivers stipulates that automobile drivers should submit their licenses to the Bureau of Public Utilities for review once every full year from the date of issuance, and pay a handling fee of one yuan each time. The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities has now found that many drivers who have been licensed for a full year have not complied with the regulations and submitted them for review. Yesterday, a special announcement was issued to all drivers that if their licenses have been issued for a year, they should submit them for review immediately, otherwise, once discovered, they will be punished in accordance with item 9 of Article 9 of the regulations.

The Issue of Chinese Nationality in Debt Cases

▲ Xu Ruilin Had Already Entered British Nationality

▲ Plaintiff's Lawyer Believes It Is Invalid

Hu Songnian, a broker at the Shanghai Chinese Stock Exchange, hired a lawyer to represent him in a lawsuit in the French court, stating that the defendants Xu Ruilin and Gao Junfeng, in the name of Chengji Trading Company, previously entrusted the plaintiff to buy and sell public bonds totaling more than 1.1 million yuan. The defendants signed a transaction note as proof. As of March 11 this year, it was calculated that they owed 48,890.64 yuan in silver. They were asked to pay, but they ignored the request, so the case was filed for prosecution. The defendant Xu Ruilin, through his lawyer, argued that his client Xu Ruilin was born in England and had long been a British citizen, and that he had a passport to prove it. The plaintiff's accusation was not within the jurisdiction of the court and should be dismissed. The plaintiff's lawyer also replied that, according to the Nationality Law, the defendant must produce a certificate of renunciation of nationality from the Ministry of the Interior for it to be effective. Since there was no certificate, it was naturally invalid. Since the defendant was born in England and is now returning to his country, he should be subject to the judgment of the court of his own country. The Nationality Law has clear regulations and cannot be considered valid based on the defendant's one-sided statement. He requested a clear investigation. The defendant Gao Junfeng also defended everything through his lawyer. Judge Gong ordered them to leave and wait for a decision on the nationality issue before further investigation.

Failure to Redeem Property Deeds on Time

▲ Chinese Business Company Files a Complaint

▲ Requesting Permission to Dispose of the Collateral

The land broker Zhang Wenxiang mortgaged three property deeds for houses located on Zhengjia Wood Bridge in the French Concession to the American-owned Chinese Business Company for 10,000 taels of silver at the end of September last year, with an interest rate of 1% per month. Recently, because Zhang failed to redeem the deeds on time, the company hired a lawyer to sue in the Special District Local Court, requesting that the defendant be ordered to repay the principal and interest of the mortgage, or that the collateral be disposed of. If the proceeds from the auction are not enough to pay the debt, the defendant should still be required to make up the difference. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang opened a court session to summon the defendant, who also hired a lawyer to appear in court, raising the issue of jurisdiction, saying that the mortgaged property and the mortgage act were both in the French Concession, and the plaintiff should file a lawsuit in the French Concession. The plaintiff's lawyer strongly opposed this issue, saying that the plaintiff was an American businessman and operated in the Public Concession, so the case should naturally be handled by the Special District Court. Judge Yang then decided that the court had jurisdiction over the case and ordered the plaintiff to submit evidence for further investigation at a later date.

A Lawyer's Broker Forges Checks

▲ Defrauding a Deposit of 1,250 Yuan

▲ Sentenced to One Year and Two Months in Prison, Still to Appeal

Tan Zhongxi, a Guangdong native, was previously a broker at Feng Zhongba's law office on Szechuan Road. On the 12th of last month, Tan stole the lawyer's checkbook and seal, and then forged Feng's name to defraud the Guangdong Bank of 1,250 yuan of Feng's deposit. After being discovered, it was reported to the General Police Station, and Tan was arrested and detained for questioning. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen of the Special District Local Court brought Tan to trial. Feng Zhongba testified that the defendant had fraudulently obtained his deposit and requested punishment. Tan denied everything, saying that he had a quarrel with Feng.

Page 16

Because Tan Zhongxi reported that the signature on the check signed by the defendant was confirmed to be the defendant's handwriting after being enlarged by photography. Judge Shen immediately sentenced Tan Zhongxi to one year and two months in prison. Tan's attorney stated in court that Tan was not satisfied and requested permission to appeal, so the case cannot yet be considered closed.

Attention Ship Owners Anchoring in Ports

▲ Must Leave Immediately When the Whistle Sounds

▲ No Responsibility for Collisions If Not Obeyed

Various ship companies along the southern city's riverbank have investigated and found that the equipment at each wharf was originally intended for merchant ships to drop anchor when arriving at the port. However, various types of vessels often compete to moor and line up outside the outer defenses of the port terminals. When the merchant ships of each company arrive in Shanghai and turn around to dock at the terminals prepared by the company, the various vessels do not rush to leave the docks even after hearing the sound of the whistle, but instead continue to moor as before, without moving at all. As a result, collisions occur from time to time. Therefore, each of the ship companies contacted each other and proposed methods to ban this behavior. Yesterday, they jointly submitted a petition to the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, stating the various hazards and requesting that all ship owners be notified. It was stated that if shipowners continue to disobey in the future, the companies will not be responsible for any collisions that occur.

Punishment for Failure to Affix Stamps to Account Books

The Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau has been sending inspectors to check stamps in the Nanhui Ferry area of ​​Pudong in recent days. The inspection has been quite strict. A total of five shops were found to be in violation of regulations. The account books and other items were taken back for separate punishment. Yesterday, the Third District Public Security Bureau was notified to send police to enforce the penalties. The penalized establishments are as follows: (1) Dachang Nanhua Store was found to have two account books without stamps, fined 10 yuan. (2) Guangtaichang Cigarette Shop was found to have three stamped account books without seals and signatures, fined 10 yuan. (3) Hongfaxiang Cigarette Paper Shop was found to have two unstamped account books, fined 10 yuan. (4) Xinglong Socks Shop was found to have two understamped books, fined 10 yuan. (5) Datonghe Nanhua Store was found to have one unstamped account book and one license, fined a total of 15 yuan.

Banning Women from Singing in the Streets

The Shanghai Special Municipal Public Security Bureau issued an announcement yesterday, stating, "The police have the responsibility to correct customs, because customs are the manifestation of social morality. Bad customs should be strictly prohibited and gradually eliminated in order to bring them into line with the right path and jointly promote enlightenment. Recently, in various restaurants and taverns in this city, young women often bring young girls, holding playbills in their hands, and ask the guests to order songs, which is extremely frivolous, corrupts customs, and harms morals. In addition to issuing orders to the various districts to strictly prohibit this, a public announcement is made for everyone to know. From now on, if the aforementioned circumstances occur again, once discovered, severe punishment will be imposed without leniency. Everyone must comply and not violate this announcement."

Lawsuit for Cohabitation with a Lieutenant's Wife

▲ Allowance of 12 Yuan Per Month

▲ On-the-Spot Reconciliation Achieved

Ji Hanwenshu, a young woman from Anhui, recently hired lawyers Jin Yu and Li Yuan to sue her husband, Ji Kegong, in the Shanghai Local Court for abandonment and to demand cohabitation. The wording of the complaint stated, "On the 29th day of the tenth month of the lunar calendar in the 17th year of the Republic of China, I married the defendant, Ji Kegong, through a matchmaker. Unexpectedly, only six days after the marriage, on the fifth day of the eleventh month, the defendant went to work in the army in Hankou. Since then, he has repeatedly sent letters to his parents-in-law and the plaintiff, requesting a divorce. On the 27th day of the second month of last year, the defendant finally came to Shanghai, but he did not often talk to the plaintiff. At that time, the defendant was infected with syphilis and was only cured in April. Then he went out again. The plaintiff had no choice but to rely on her elder brother and sister-in-law for a living and requested a court judgment." Yesterday afternoon at 2 o'clock, Judge Wang specially opened the Fourth Court for trial. The plaintiff, Ji Hanwenshu, stated that she was 24 years old, from Anhui, and recounted the previous events. She also said, "Now, whether the defendant wants me or not, I am determined to become a nun." The judge repeatedly tried to persuade her. The plaintiff also said, "The defendant must work in Shanghai." The judge questioned the defendant, Ji Kegong, who stated that he was 25 years old, from Shanghai, residing in Longhua West Town, and currently working in the Wireless Telegraph First Battalion of the First Regiment of the Transportation Corps of the Commander-in-Chief of the Land and Sea Forces in Xuzhou (as a lieutenant), with a monthly salary of 42 yuan. At this point, the plaintiff submitted many letters from the defendant requesting a divorce, requesting the court to investigate. She also said, "The defendant has someone else he likes in Hanyang, Hubei. She is a woman from Sichuan, as told to me by the defendant's younger brother. I don't think it's false." The judge asked the defendant if this was true, and he replied, "No, but now that social interaction between men and women is open, there may be female colleagues traveling with me at work, which cannot be immediately interpreted as improper." He continued, "Now that the plaintiff is requesting to live together again, I am willing." The judge then said to the plaintiff, "I order the defendant to pay you a living allowance of 12 yuan per month." The plaintiff replied, "Twelve yuan is not enough, because I need to study now, because the defendant dislikes that I am illiterate." The judge said, "Don't deliberately make things difficult," and gave the plaintiff various analogies. The plaintiff nodded in agreement, and a reconciliation was achieved. The defendant will pay the plaintiff a living allowance of 12 yuan per month by the end of each month. The judge wrote a reconciliation record and ordered both parties to sign it. All the letters submitted by the plaintiff were returned in court. The defendant requested that the letters be burned in court, but the plaintiff refused. The judge said that since a reconciliation had been reached, there were no issues with the letters, and then adjourned the court.

Xiao Lanzi Does Not Want to Marry a Country Bumpkin

▲ Sues for Dissolution of Marriage

Zhu Xiao Lanzi, a 22-year-old woman from Gaoyou, was betrothed at the age of 17 to Zuo Da, a villager from the Bansongyuan area of Shanghai. Last year, Xiao Lanzi came to Shanghai and worked as a maid for a family surnamed 某 in Shaoqing Lane on Rue Lafayette. Influenced by what she saw and heard, she no longer wanted to return to her hometown. She hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the local court requesting the dissolution of the marriage, claiming that the betrothal was made without her consent and was a completely autocratic marriage in the form of a sale. The plaintiff has been working as a maid in Shanghai for five years since the age of 17. She has heard that the defendant intends to forcibly marry her, so she has come to court to request permission to dissolve the marriage. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, Judge Zhang opened a court session to examine the case. The plaintiff, Zhu Xiao Lanzi, stated that she was 22 years old, from Gaoyou, and had parents at home. She stated, "I didn't know about the betrothal until now. I only learned that my parents had betrothed me to the defendant, but I do not agree to this marriage." (Question) "Do you know the defendant?" (Answer) "I don't know him. I returned home from Shanghai last May and declared to my mother that I was unwilling." The judge said, "If you were unwilling, why didn't you file a lawsuit at that time?" (Answer) "I didn't know how to file a lawsuit at that time." The judge ordered the defendant to take the stand. The defendant stated that he was 24 years old and that he had betrothed the plaintiff in the fifth month of the 14th year of the Republic of China. At that time, the plaintiff was still at home and should have known. He also stated that the plaintiff's father was waiting outside the door for instructions. The judge then ordered the plaintiff's father, Zhu Zhaoxing, to be brought to the stand. He stated that he was 43 years old and farmed in his hometown. (Question) "When did Xiao Lanzi come to Shanghai?" (Answer) "She only came to Shanghai last June." (Question) "Has she been here before?" (Answer) "She came to Shanghai once before in the 17th year of the Republic of China. She had never been here before." (Question) "Was your daughter willing when she was betrothed?" (Answer) "My daughter was also willing. Moreover, we are old relatives. But a daughter cannot marry two husbands." (Question) "Do you know about your daughter's lawsuit this time?" (Answer) "I don't know. I just came to Shanghai today." After obtaining the statements, the judge advised the plaintiff not to dissolve the marriage. However, Xiao Lanzi claimed, "I don't want to marry him. I must choose my own marriage." Her father, Zhu Zhaoxing, who was listening nearby, immediately scolded his daughter, saying, "You beast, I raised you to be so big, and you want to make your own decisions. Is there any reason in the world?" The judge then advised both parties to go outside and reconcile. If a reconciliation could not be reached, the case would be reconvened and a judgment would be made according to law. After leaving the court, the defendant's father grabbed his daughter and pushed her into a rickshaw, heading south.

Mrs. Tang Yang's Husband is Available to Everyone

▲ Discovered Inside Room 13 of the Laian Hotel

Mrs. Tang Yang, a 24-year-old woman from Hangzhou, is quite beautiful. Her husband, Tang Cailin, lives outside Qingbomen in Hangzhou and makes a living by growing vegetables. The relationship between the couple is not harmonious. In recent years, Mrs. Tang has been learning to be fashionable and dislikes her husband's rudeness. She wants to find a good husband, so she entrusted someone to recommend her to the silk reeling department of the Jiaxing Weicheng Company as a silk reeling worker. Before long, she fell in love with a soldier named Yang. Yang's appearance and temperament are far superior to her husband, so she wants to live together for a long time. Fearing that the affair would be exposed, Mrs. Tang and her lover Yang agreed to live in Shanghai. Mrs. Tang first took a train to Shanghai, and Yang agreed to come the next morning and meet at the North Station. After Mrs. Tang arrived in Shanghai, she waited at the station the next morning as agreed. Unexpectedly, her lover broke the agreement. From morning to night, she did not see him arrive in Shanghai. Mrs. Tang had no choice but to say that she had something to do in Shanghai and stayed with her husband's elder brother, Tang Zhaolin, for one night. The next day, she went to the station to wait again, eagerly hoping, but Yang did not come for a long time. Mrs. Tang wandered around the station, craning her neck to look every time a train arrived, sometimes talking to herself, looking like she was waiting for her lover. At that time, Li Hongfa (29 years old) from Hunan was looking around, saw Mrs. Tang's situation, and came forward to ask her kindly. Sure enough, she was waiting for her lover. Li recommended himself, saying that his wife had died of illness and he lacked someone to take care of his household, so he wanted to find a suitable person to continue the marriage. He seduced her in every way. Mrs. Tang thought that Yang was ungrateful and broke the agreement. She was in a foreign land and did not know what to do. Seeing that Li's appearance was not bad and that he had no wife, she thought that he could be a long-term husband. So she went to a nearby hotel with him, swore oaths of love, and had illicit relations for seven days and nights. Li was a licentious man and his finances were insufficient, and he gradually became embarrassed. Since Mrs. Tang was originally a female worker, they agreed that Mrs. Tang would enter the Eternal 永 Spinning Factory and be a wonderful female worker. However, Mrs. Tang could not endure the hardship. After working for seven days, she returned to Shanghai with Li and entered the Laian Hotel at the North Station, opening room 13. In the evening, Wu Xin, a patrol officer from the first division of the fourth district, led police officer Liu Haishan to the hotel for inspection. Seeing that Li and Mrs. Tang did not look like a formal couple, they questioned them and their speech was evasive. They were taken to the division station. According to Mrs. Yang's statement, she was cohabiting with Li Hongfa. While the investigation was underway, Tang Zhaolin heard the news and reported to the division that Li had seduced his sister-in-law, requesting an investigation. The division chief, Ni Wenbiao, thought that the case was complicated and ordered that a document be prepared and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Cause of Death of a Woman Unknown

Dong A'gen, a Cantonese cook on a ship traveling to Swatow on Shanghai Road, lives at 98 Gongping Road. His wife, Li, is addicted to gambling and has accumulated a lot of debt. A'gen returned home the day before yesterday and, after learning about the situation, argued with her. She then went upstairs, and A'gen also went out. Soon after, the second landlord, Chen Song, went upstairs and saw that her face had changed drastically, as if she had taken poison. She reported it to the Hongkou police station and ordered the detectives to send her to the hospital for treatment. She died not long after. The police sent the body to the forensic center on Philand Road. Yesterday morning, the Special District Local Court appointed Prosecutor Guo to examine the body at the forensic center. Chen Song stated that she did not know the cause of death. However, she saw her vomit a lot of black liquid at the time and did not know if she had taken opium. There was no opium box or smoking equipment in her room. According to the sister of the deceased, Chen Li, who also arrived at the scene, there was nothing that could prove the cause of death. Prosecutor Guo then issued a written order stating that the cause of death of the deceased woman Dong Li was unknown and should be examined by the court police and the hospital doctor of the Bureau of Public Works. The case was adjourned to next Monday for further questioning.

▲ Entrusts Neighbor to Take Good Care of Her Child

▲ Overdose of Poison, Life in Danger

Zhao A'liu, a Cantonese man in his late thirties who lives upstairs in a semi-finished clothing store at 39 Miller Road in Hongkou, has been working at the Jiangnan Shipbuilding Plant in Gaochang Temple in this city. Twenty years ago, he married a woman surnamed Huang from his hometown, who is now 37 years old. They have only one son, named A'si, who is 20 years old. Last year, Zhao had an affair with a woman outside, and their relationship was very close, which caused him not to return home often. Later, his wife found out and repeatedly quarreled with Zhao. The day before yesterday (the 17th), another dispute broke out, followed by violence. The neighbors came out to mediate, and the matter was settled. That night, Zhao went out and did not return. His wife was depressed and, the night before last (the 18th) at 9 o'clock, secretly swallowed opium paste to commit suicide. She also told the neighbor that A'si, the child, should be taken care of at any time. It was not until yesterday morning that someone noticed it and immediately sent her to the Tongren Hospital for treatment. Due to the long-term overdose, her life is in danger.

Sun Xunqiu's Inheritance Lawsuit

▲ Judge Advised to Consider the Brotherhood

▲ Hoping that Both Parties Would Settle Amicably

Hu Sun Jinghua, the married daughter of the late wealthy merchant Sun Xunqiu, and her brothers Sun Zhongwei and Zhongyao, etc., were involved in a lawsuit in the Special District Local Court over the possession of inheritance. It was reported in the previous newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yang Yi opened a court session to continue the trial. Song Mingdong, the lawyer representing the plaintiff, stated the facts of the case, saying that Sun Xunqiu passed away in January of the 17th year of the Republic of China, and his inheritance was divided by the defendants in March of that year, as evidenced by a draft agreement. The plaintiff now requests a re-division based on the provision that married daughters have the right to inherit the estate. In the defendant's defense statement, it was stated that most of Xunqiu's inheritance was divided as early as the 14th year, which is not true. The draft agreement presented in the case is a method of pre-distribution and cannot prove that it has been divided. The traceability clause clearly states that it should be based on the commencement of inheritance, and the commencement of inheritance should be calculated from the date of death of the deceased. The analysis cannot be used as a synonym for inheritance. The analysis and inheritance are two different things. Even if the analysis is in the past, the commencement of inheritance is always after the new interpretation takes effect. Therefore, the plaintiff's claim to re-analyze is in accordance with the law. Yuan Hanyun, the lawyer representing the defendant, then rebutted the plaintiff's lawyer's statements one by one and presented various evidences to prove that Xunqiu's inheritance was indeed divided in the 14th year. At that time, the resolution on women inheriting inheritance had not taken effect in Jiangsu Province, and the plaintiff had no right to claim it. He requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be rejected. Judge Yang then questioned the defendants and advised both parties to consider the brotherhood and resolve the matter peacefully to avoid hurting feelings. The case was adjourned, and if the two parties could not reach a settlement, it would be investigated further.

Li Quanshi's Important Remarks on Education Funding ▲ Central and Local Governments Should Increase Funding ▲ There are Three Measures in Total The review committees of all groups of the National Education Conference have convened meetings for review one after another, except for the Education Funding Group, which has not yet begun its review. Funding is the mother of fact; if the funding issue cannot be resolved, the proposals of each group will become empty talk on paper. Yesterday, the reporter specifically inquired about this matter from the expert member of the Education Funding Committee, Dr. Li Quanshi. According to him, there is indeed a solution to the entire funding issue for improving the national education plan. The date for the Education Funding Review Group's meeting will be after each group has completed its review, and one representative will be selected from each group to participate in the discussion. Therefore, the parts of each group's review report concerning funding will be reserved for the Education Funding Review Group to review in the future before being submitted to the General Assembly for approval. The following are the central and local governments' annual increases in education funding (approximate figures in millions of yuan) after the national education improvement plan is passed, as discussed by Mr. Li: Year Central Province County/City 1st 30 6 26 2nd 37 17 32 3rd 52 16 54 4th 58 18 62 5th 65 19 69 6th 79 23 84 7th 89 25 94 8th 98 27 105 9th 108 29 115 10th 117 31 126 11th 140 33 136 12th 35 147 13th 146 37 157 14th 156 40 167 15th 166 42 177 16th 175 44 188 17th 185 46 199 18th 194 48 109 19th 204 50 220 20th 213 52 230 As for the methods of increasing education funding, the central government can rectify or increase the following taxes: (A) Ability tax (including income tax and inheritance tax), (B) Benefit tax, indirect consumption tax, reform of salt tax, | tax collection at the market; the provincial government can increase benefit tax, business tax; the county and city can increase ability tax, income tax surcharge, central inheritance tax subsidies, (C) Benefit tax, direct consumption tax, banquet tax. The Nationality Issue of Establishing Elementary Schools and Kindergartens ▲ In the preliminary review, Article 6 under the establishment section was removed | Vigorous discussion tomorrow | At the fourth general meeting, the preliminary review committee decided to remove Article 6 under the establishment section of the plan to improve elementary education: "Groups organized by non-Chinese people or not entirely by Chinese people shall not be allowed to establish elementary schools and kindergartens. Teachers and staff of elementary schools and kindergartens shall be limited to people who are completely citizens of the Republic of China." This will lead to a fierce debate. Some members said that the review committee is based on the principle of promoting compulsory education and advocates deletion, while the opposition stands on the party's position, based on the educational goals of the Republic of China, promoting national spirit, and resisting cultural aggression, advocating maintaining the original proposal of the Ministry of Education. It is still known that basic education should be run by Chinese people themselves. Everyone knows that the basic education of a country should be handled by its own people. This is a matter of course. Educational policy, needless to say, we Chinese people formulate education plans for Chinese people, and solemnly declare that elementary schools and kindergartens should be run by Chinese people. It has already followed the same path as the saying "there are no foreign three hundred taels of silver inside the house," revealing our weakness and showing that the education of us Chinese people is mostly contracted by foreigners. But it is barely satisfactory. Everyone still thinks that foreign-run schools in China should be taken back. Therefore, a provision was specifically made that groups not organized by citizens of the Republic of China or not entirely by citizens of the Republic of China shall not be allowed to establish elementary schools and kindergartens. Who knows that the review committee deleted this provision? I personally think that it is either because there is no money to take back these many foreign-run schools, or it is feared that the implementation of compulsory education will be hindered. If it is for the former, then there is no need to set out the limit for the realization of compulsory education; if it is for the latter, then it can be easily solved. Isn't it possible to first recover these many foreign-established schools by preparing the first phase of compulsory education funding? In short, setting out the principle that Chinese people should run schools for Chinese people in the plan is already a low standard. After it has been set out, it is still reviewed and deleted, especially leading to a dead end, making people puzzled, and doing something unnecessary. I don’t know what many problems will arise. The most important one is the issue of national independence and the policy of cultural aggression. I deeply hope that all representatives will pay more attention to this basic education product related to the survival of the nation and promote overseas Chinese education. ▲ Zhuang Zexuan, Zheng Hongnian and others proposed a case to request the government to support the development of overseas Chinese funding to promote overseas Chinese education. Zhuang Zexuan and others proposed a case to request the government to support the development of overseas Chinese funding to promote overseas Chinese education. (Reasons) 1. According to a survey in previous years, overseas Chinese remit more than 10,000,000 yuan back to their motherland every year. In recent years, due to fierce commercial competition, the economic situation has plummeted. If measures are not taken to help them as soon as possible, not only will the 10,000,000 overseas Chinese have no place to stand overseas, but also the domestic economy will inevitably suffer a major blow. 2. Overseas Chinese are extremely enthusiastic about supporting revolutionary work, and the funds they have contributed are also considerable. When drinking water, one should think of its source. Today's government has an obligation to support the economic development of overseas Chinese. 3. In education, Xiamen University, Jimei School, etc., which were independently established and operated by overseas Chinese, are unable to maintain due to economic difficulties. Overseas Chinese education funds in the Philippines have always relied solely on business surcharges, and various schools have used this to develop. The Central Executive Committee has recognized this as a good method. Please ask overseas Chinese in various places to follow suit. Recently, due to business failures, it is impossible to implement this method that was not originally created. These two matters can prove that if the government does not take measures to support the economic development of overseas Chinese as soon as possible, the future of overseas Chinese education will be unimaginable. (Measures) 1. Please ask the National Government to issue an order to all customs offices to exempt overseas Chinese manufactured products from import and transit taxes. 2. Please ask the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to implement the selection and dispatch of commissioners as soon as possible to be stationed or travel to various places to assist overseas Chinese in developing industry and commerce. 3. Please ask the Ministry of Education to designate various universities related to overseas Chinese education to train overseas Chinese affairs cadres. 4. Please ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to be responsible for handling any foreign affairs related to overseas Chinese education quickly and properly. Proponents: Zhuang Zexuan, Zheng Hongnian, Ou Yuanhuai, Chen Dezheng, Zhao Bangfu, Qian He, Zhu Baoqin, Liu Shimu, Lei Peihong, Jin Zengcheng, Chen Bulei, etc. The proposal was approved to be submitted for discussion first. ▲ Political Conference Responds to the Ministry of Education The Central Executive Committee's Political Conference sent a letter to the Ministry of Education on the 18th, stating that the submitted education plan and general budget have been reviewed by the conference and are generally consistent with the party's platform and the resolutions on education at previous meetings, and can be submitted for discussion first. Sincerely, Political Conference of the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang, Hou Hongjian, Representative of the Fujian Provincial Department of Education, Talks ▲ The Arrest of Cheng Bai-Lu, Education, and Its Impact Hou Hongjian, representative of the Fujian Provincial Department of Education, arrived in Beijing on the 19th morning to attend the meeting and had the following conversation with reporters. The reporter asked: 1. What is the situation after Cheng Bai-Lu was arrested? Hou replied: After Director Cheng was arrested in Fujian, he was initially treated favorably in Yan, but then he was returned to the province and detained in the Hongshanqiao Arsenal. With the arrival of the 56th Division in the province, he was sent to northern Fujian for the second time, and he went deeper into the mountains, reaching Youxi. Youxi is where the Lu Division is stationed. The name is favorable treatment, but the living conditions are far worse than before. Question 2. What is the state of education in Fujian Province after Cheng was arrested? Answer: Education in Fujian Province was originally in its infancy, and the education funding was insufficient, only more than 1.4 million yuan per year. In the past three months, the Salt Affairs Inspection Office has only handed over a maximum of more than 70,000 yuan per month to the Education Funding Management Office, causing Secretary Hou to do his best to maintain it and deal with subsidies to schools inside and outside the province and counties. As of now, each is owed one or two months. The cost of studying in the East and West Oceans is owed for up to six months. Without rice to cook, Chen Peikun, director of the Management Office, resigned, and the entire education community in the province is helping. Whether the schools can continue to operate after this is still unknown until the summer vacation. Question 3. What is the impact after the arrest? Answer: After the five provincial committee members and the Water Police Bureau were arrested, the heads and supervisors of education bureaus in various counties were subjected to school closures and beatings at various schools, which is endless. The so-called "what the superiors do, the subordinates follow" and the mutual contention for power make education impossible to speak of. The finances cannot be collected, and there is no way to obtain education funds. Administrative expenses are owed for two or three months. What can be said about chaos and profit? Detailed Account of the Examination Yuan's Banquet ▲ Dai Jitao and Cai Yuanpei Both Gave Speeches ▲ Members Publicly Elected Jin Zengcheng to Deliver a Reply On the evening of the 18th, at 7:30, the Examination Yuan hosted a banquet for the members of the National Education Conference, which was recorded in yesterday's newspaper. The details are now recorded below. More than a hundred people, including Cai Yuanpei, Yang Xingfo, and Jiang Menglin, attended that evening, and were received by Dai Jitao, Shao Yuanchong, Zhang Mojun, etc. At about 8:00, they entered the seats. At the end of the banquet, Dai stood up and gave a speech, saying roughly that today the Examination Yuan is holding a banquet for all representatives and experts. We are very happy to have you all here. In the past few decades, the political employment and administration in our country have lacked standards, so politics has become increasingly bleak. The task of the Examination Yuan is to remedy this shortcoming. Judging from the current situation in China, the implementation of examinations is truly urgent. Moreover, examinations are one of the important proposals of Mr. Sun Yat-sen during his lifetime. Mr. Sun Yat-sen's most important remarks on examinations are the three words: "Cultivate properly, encourage properly, and employ appropriately." The work of political testing and appointment focuses on the second and third sentences, while the work of the first sentence is the responsibility of the education sector. After all, the government's employment and administration are not successful without relying on examination work, but if you want the examination to obtain appropriate talents, then you must rely on the education sector. At present, in the political field, from the central government to local autonomy, there is a feeling of a lack of talent, especially in local autonomy. In each village, it is impossible to find literate people, so the government's orders cannot be directly communicated to the people everywhere. Even if the government has the most complete policies, it is equivalent to setting up a shell. In the future, all civil servants in all provinces and counties must pass the examination. If education is not properly conducted, then there will be no appropriate talents to take the examination. From now on, if you want to seek progress in all aspects of politics and society, you must rely on good education, and if you want to seek progress in education, you must have a systematic and comprehensive plan. Although the resolutions of the First National Education Conference were also excellent and complete, the shortcoming was that the opinions of all parties were lost in the resolutions. Therefore, when implemented, there were disadvantages of not knowing what to do. This time, the proposal was formulated by the central government with a concrete plan in advance, and then the opinions of various experts and representatives were collected. It is expected that there will be more satisfactory results. Today, I would like to briefly state my views on the tasks of the Examination Yuan to all educators. As for the hospitality, because it was sudden, there were many inadequacies, please forgive me. The members publicly elected Jin Zengcheng to deliver a reply, saying roughly that Mr. Dai is an advanced educator, and his remarks and contributions to education have been extensively reported in domestic newspapers and magazines. The education community has long admired him in their hearts. Today, my colleagues and others have the honor to hear his teachings, which is a great honor. In the future, if there is an opportunity, please ask Mr. Dai to come to the conference and give a speech. I would like to toast Mr. Dai this glass of wine and offer a cup to Mr. Dai. Mr. Cai Yuanpei's speech: Just now Mr. Dai spoke to all the members from the standpoint of the Examination Yuan. I greatly admire him. Shantou Boy Scouts Arrive The 73rd Regiment directly under the Boy Scout Headquarters, that is, the Shantou Youlian, is cultivating talents. Whether the talents cultivated in schools can be used by society depends on the Examination Yuan. The Examination Yuan has the function of selecting talents created by educational institutions. The educational situation in China is slightly different from that of other countries in the world. In Chinese schools, students can always graduate at the end of their years in school. If they are not allowed to graduate, the students will quarrel with the school authorities endlessly. Operators can generally know this. There are many ways to remedy this problem, such as organizing a committee, with teachers from other schools presiding over the examination, etc., but it is not as good as having the Examination Yuan preside over it. Now Japan, Belgium, etc. have implemented it. The examination authority presides over the school examination. It seems that our country can also imitate it. In this way, educational institutions can relax the method of interfering with unofficial schools. This time, because the period is different from before, the central government formulated the general plan and handed it over to the conference for discussion. The final decision is still up to the central government. Mr. Dai's proposal in the past has now been fully realized. This method is very good, because of the free development of personality, it has been done once before. The advantage of this method is that it can concentrate attention and focus the spirit, which is most convenient and effective for discussion. This is my personal feeling. Last time, Mr. Dai was in Guangdong. This time, Mr. Dai is in the capital. He will definitely give us the opportunity to guide us. New Contributions from National Education Experts ▲ The Student Guide is Popular Throughout the Country More than 30 national education experts, including Ou Yuanhuai, Liao Maoru, Zheng Hongnian, Li Quanshi, Jiang Wenyu, and Liu Zhanen, jointly wrote the "Student Guide" to meet the needs of the national student community. Since its publication, it has been popular throughout the country. The content is divided into two volumes, upper and lower. The upper volume guides the study paths of college students, middle school students, female students, overseas Chinese students, foreign students, and students in various colleges of liberal arts, law, business, agriculture, medicine, and normal schools, as well as the training of Boy Scout education, etc. The lower volume guides the methods of studying Chinese studies, English studies, social sciences, economics, mass education, vocational education, art, painting, music, dance, and translation, as well as physical education and health matters, further education, career selection, and personal conduct. All problems are described in detail and guided by chapters. It is truly the crystallization of the efforts of all the experts. Its precious value can be imagined. For students, having this book is like meeting each educator in a room and listening to their teachings every day. The whole book is one inch thick, more than 500 pages, beautifully bound, and comes with portraits and biographies of the authors. The price is two yuan, but it is now sold at a special price of 1.2 yuan. It is published by Qinfen Bookstore at No. 39 Xinmin Village, Malin Road, French Concession, Shanghai, and distributed by Xie Wenyi Printing House, Wangping Street, Shanghai. Major bookstores in Shanghai, such as the World, Datong, and Wenming, all have it for sale, and bookstores in other places also sell it on consignment.
